        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2331106885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2073362768095703304">This is a story of the Borgias told through the eyes of Sancha of Aragon. She is sent to marry the "son" of Pope Alexander VI, Jofre for political reasons. I had to wonder at first if this was where George R. R. Martin got the names for the characters in Game of Thrones. She gets caught up in the evilness of the Borgia family and their quest to rule all of Italy. What a horrible, disgusting family they were, but the story was riveting. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17330192832243310453">Warning: This book does contain explicit sex and rape scenes. <br/><br/>I picked this up at Half Price Books, expecting a quick historical retelling. What I ended up with was a nuanced, fairly accurate (from my admittedly limited knowledge), sympathetic retelling of Sancha of Aragon's tragic story. The tone of the novel changes from the bright, simple naivete of a young woman who is ready to be married, to that of a hardened and grieving woman who suffered through the ravages of the Borgia court. It deftl</span>
  <span id="freeText17330192832243310453" style="display:none">Warning: This book does contain explicit sex and rape scenes. <br /><br />I picked this up at Half Price Books, expecting a quick historical retelling. What I ended up with was a nuanced, fairly accurate (from my admittedly limited knowledge), sympathetic retelling of Sancha of Aragon's tragic story. The tone of the novel changes from the bright, simple naivete of a young woman who is ready to be married, to that of a hardened and grieving woman who suffered through the ravages of the Borgia court. It deftly weaves the political and historical facts with the personal perspective of someone who would have lived through the times.<br /><br />One thing I particularly loved was the novel's rendering of its female characters, and that it makes the reader reexamine how women were treated and manipulated in what was absolutely a man's world...and how they could find power in that world.</span>

<div id="review_124947929" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/124947929" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2160730-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301322622p2/2160730.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/124947929?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/2160730-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer124947929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10940454600823425979">I had read a few reviews of this book before I started it. And even seeing mention how scandalous the Borgia family was, I don't think I believed that that would in fact turn out to be the case. BOY! Was I ever wrong! Even with all of that going on it was still a very interesting novel. Very hard to put down, kind of like a train wreck you can't help but look at? It was very much like that. <br/><br/>I picked this book up, having read another one of Ms. Kalogridis' books before. And I admit to being curio</span>
  <span id="freeText10940454600823425979" style="display:none">I had read a few reviews of this book before I started it. And even seeing mention how scandalous the Borgia family was, I don't think I believed that that would in fact turn out to be the case. BOY! Was I ever wrong! Even with all of that going on it was still a very interesting novel. Very hard to put down, kind of like a train wreck you can't help but look at? It was very much like that. <br /><br />I picked this book up, having read another one of Ms. Kalogridis' books before. And I admit to being curious about the Borgia's on a whole. Especially once I learned that the Borgia apartments in the Vatican had been sealed for some time. What sort of scandal could have caused that? Well, this book will tell you what sort of scandal caused this! <br /><br />I enjoyed Sancha's character very much. Although at times I thought she was a little too worried about going mad. I understand that since her father and grandfather were off kilter that she might head that way also, but so could anyone else in her family. So I thought that obsession was a little bit much. I liked the way the war in Naples was described, and how much it showed that the younger generation just wanted to go home, and restore their birthright. <br /><br />I did not care for Jofre at all. His was a character that I tried again and again to like in some way. And I just couldn't do it. He was her husband, but he was so weak, and undecided most of the time. It was easy to see how he was used as a pawn and ridiculed by his family. I don't doubt that he cared very much for Sancha and was happy to have her for his wife. He did seem quite devoted to her. Although if he was so devoted why all the courtesans? Why not stand up for her with his family? Maybe if he had a little more steel in his back bone they wouldn't have looked down on him so. <br /><br />Rodrigo Borgia was something else all together. He loved his children immensely. He came across as most content when his children were surrounding him. On that same note, he loved his daughter especially inappropriately! And for a new bride to the family to happen across the Pope and her sister-in-law (his daughter) in an "intimate embrace"....oh my goodness! <br /><br />I both liked and disliked Cesare. I thought he had good points, and then seemed to not care to cultivate them, maybe? He could have been a good man, he had the tools, but he chose to go another way. I think almost limitless power will do that to you. <br /><br />I felt sorry for Lucrezia in a way. She was obviously well used by the men in her family which is incredibly sad. And it seemed to weigh on her conscious. But, it didn't seem like she tried to ever say "No". Maybe she was too scared for her life? Maybe she didn't realize that she could in fact say no. I don't know. It was just a sad situation. <br /><br />It amazes me that this powerful family was as dastardly as it was. I'm surprised anyone lived to hear about any of the things that went on during that time. It also makes me wonder if anything could have been done to stop the destruction before it got so out of hand. <br /><br />Over all, very good read. Ms. Kalogridis does not disappoint! </span>
  <a data-text-id="10940454600823425979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_76174693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76174693" />
    <a title="PurplyCookie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie"><img alt="PurplyCookie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415491715p2/2214498.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76174693?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="PurplyCookie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="PurplyCookie" href="/user/show/2214498-purplycookie">PurplyCookie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=biography-memoir">biography-memoir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2214498-purplycookie?shelf=royalty">royalty</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76174693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11167584178558544137">Against the backdrop of 15th-century Italian feuds, debauchery and Vatican corruption, <b>"The Borgia Bride"</b> chronicles the story of the ravishing and iron-willed Sancha de Aragon, princess of Naples. Illegitimate daughter to the cold-hearted Duke of Calabria (briefly king of Naples), she is used to establish ties to the feared and influential House of Borgia when her father betroths her to the younger scion, Jofre. <br/><br/>Much to the dismay of her beloved younger brother Alfonso, Sancha is sent from Napl</span>
  <span id="freeText11167584178558544137" style="display:none">Against the backdrop of 15th-century Italian feuds, debauchery and Vatican corruption, <b>"The Borgia Bride"</b> chronicles the story of the ravishing and iron-willed Sancha de Aragon, princess of Naples. Illegitimate daughter to the cold-hearted Duke of Calabria (briefly king of Naples), she is used to establish ties to the feared and influential House of Borgia when her father betroths her to the younger scion, Jofre. <br /><br />Much to the dismay of her beloved younger brother Alfonso, Sancha is sent from Naples to rule with Prince Jofre in remote Squillace. War with the French will later briefly return her to Naples, but rumors of her beauty reach her lecherous father-in-law, Pope Alexander VI, who recalls her and Jofre to opulent Rome. There, she avoids the pope's advances—and her jealous sister-in-law Lucrezia's animosity—but falls into a steamy affair with her brother-in-law, the dashing Cesare, cardinal of Valencia. Cesare becomes furious when she refuses to leave Jofre, and he sets out on a warpath that includes her brother Alfonso, who has also married into the Borgia clan—to Lucrezia. <br /><br />The Borgia family, bloodthirsty and monstrous, and the era of Savonarola, Macchiavelli and Leonardo da Vinci cannot fail to fascinate. While the story was set during a fascinating historical era of Italian and Papal history with the infamous Borgia family center stage, it provides a fascinating view of the decadence and what could be construed as a prime example of the term dysfunctional family. Kalogridis took a lot of liberties in fleshing out the characters but I think she was still within the realm of historical accuracy. This is a work of fiction and I believe not everything has to be exact. <br /><br /><br /><u>Book Details: </u><br /><br /><u>Title</u> The Borgia Bride<br /><u>Author</u> Jeanne Kalogridis <br /><u>Reviewed By</u> Purplycookie</span>
  <a data-text-id="11167584178558544137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_89666780" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89666780" />
    <a title="Marie Z. Johansen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1504286-marie-z-johansen"><img alt="Marie Z. Johansen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574794558p2/1504286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89666780?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marie Z. Johansen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marie Z. Johansen" href="/user/show/1504286-marie-z-johansen">Marie Z. Johansen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1504286-marie-z-johansen?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89666780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4552174263140966978">I had had this book on my shelf for a bit and decided it was time to read it. I'm glad I did. This novel follows the life of a Bride to the powerful Borgia family. Ms. Kalogridis' summary of the book states:<br/><br/><br/>"...THE BORGIA BRIDE is a sumptuous historical novel of passion, betrayal, scheming and incest, set in the Vatican during the 15th century, one of the most exciting, violent and also sensual times of European history. The plot and characters are based on actual historical personages and event</span>
  <span id="freeText4552174263140966978" style="display:none">I had had this book on my shelf for a bit and decided it was time to read it. I'm glad I did. This novel follows the life of a Bride to the powerful Borgia family. Ms. Kalogridis' summary of the book states:<br /><br /><br />"...THE BORGIA BRIDE is a sumptuous historical novel of passion, betrayal, scheming and incest, set in the Vatican during the 15th century, one of the most exciting, violent and also sensual times of European history. The plot and characters are based on actual historical personages and events..."<br /><br /><br />I agree that this book is, to my mind, unique. I have not read many books that focus on the political turmoil of the 15th century in Italy. Oddly enough I have always thought that it was Lucrezia Borgia who had the reputation for using the family recipe for poison. Read this book for another theory! I sailed through the first part of this book - reading late into the night. Mid story slowed a bit for me - but the pace picked up again for a rousing final quarter of the book. The characters in The Borgia Bride are well crafted and carried through a plot that is well thought out expertly crafted with many unusual twists and turns. <br /><br /><br />This book makes me want to read all of Ms. Kalodridis' titles. I thoroughly enjoyed this book and would have gone for 5 stars - except for the lag midway through. I don;t think that you would regret reading this fine novel - it's appeal would, obviously, be for anyone who enjoys historical fiction - especially for 15th century Italy - but it would also please any lover of well crafted, fast paced fiction!<br /><br /> <br /><br />Ms. Kalogridis has an excellent website too - have a look : <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://jeannekalogridis.com/">http://jeannekalogridis.com/</a><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4552174263140966978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('XHVJlxcVwRlyj1gng6SRE+rCuTnWiPsuir1pxDxBIEdSBAtLvJWcEvZs5iQCOU0W/UeQ5HlkSoC5amZl/8RGGQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

To some she was the ruthless queen who led France into an era of savage violence. To others she was the passionate savior of the French monarchy. Acclaimed author C. W. Gortner brings Catherine to life in her own voice, allowing us to enter into the intimate world of a woman whose determination to protect her family’s throne and realm plunged her into a lethal struggle for power.  The last legitimate descendant of the illustrious Medici line, Catherine suffers the expulsion of her family from her native Florence and narrowly escapes death at the hands of an enraged mob. While still a teenager, she is betrothed to Henri, son of François I of France, and sent from Italy to an unfamiliar realm where she is overshadowed and humiliated by her husband’s lifelong mistress. Ever resilient, Catherine strives to create a role for herself through her patronage of the famous clairvoyant Nostradamus and her own innate gift as a seer. But in her fortieth year, Catherine is widowed, left alone with six young children as regent of a kingdom torn apart by religious discord and the ambitions of a treacherous nobility. Relying on her tenacity, wit, and uncanny gift for compromise, Catherine seizes power, intent on securing the throne for her sons. She allies herself with the enigmatic Protestant leader Coligny, with whom she shares an intimate secret, and implacably carves a path toward peace, unaware that her own dark fate looms before her—a fate that, if she is to save France, will demand the sacrifice of her ideals, her reputation, and the passion of her embattled heart. From the fairy-tale châteaux of the Loire Valley to the battlefields of the wars of religion to the mob-filled streets of Paris, The Confessions of Catherine de Medici is the extraordinary untold journey of one of the most maligned and misunderstood women An<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText17739704143923415207\" style=\"display:none\">The year is 1570, and in the convent of Santa Caterina, in the Italian city of Ferrara, noblewomen find space to pursue their lives under God\'s protection. But any community, however smoothly run, suffers tremors when it takes in someone by force. And the arrival of Santa Caterina\'s new novice sets in motion a chain of events that will shake the convent to its core.Ripped by her family from an illicit love affair, sixteen-year-old Serafina is willful, emotional, sharp, and defiant, young enough to have a life to look forward to and old enough to know when that life is being cut short. Her first night inside the walls is spent in an incandescent rage so violent that the dispensary mistress, Suora Zuana, is dispatched to the girl\'s cell to sedate her. Thus begins a complex relationship of trust and betrayal between the young rebel and the clever, scholarly nun, for whom the girl becomes the daughter she will never have.As Serafina rails against her incarceration, others are drawn into the drama: the ancient, mysterious Suora Magdalena, with her history of visions and ecstasies, locked in her cell; the ferociously devout novice mistress Suora Umiliana, who comes to see in the postulant a way to extend her influence; and, watching it all, the abbess, Madonna Chiara, a woman as fluent in politics as she is in prayer. As disorder and rebellion mount, it is the abbess\'s job to keep the convent stable while, outside its walls, the dictates of the Counter-Reformation begin to purge the Catholic Church and impose on the nunneries a regime of terrible oppression.Sarah Dunant, the bestselling author of The Birth of Venus and In the Company of the Courtesan, brings this intricate Renaissance world compellingly to life.
